    1473             : /**********************************************************************
    1474             :  *                   TABFontPoint::GetFontStyleMIFValue()
    1475             :  *
    1476             :  * Return the Font Style value for this object using the style values
    1477             :  * that are used in a MIF FONT() clause.  See MIF specs (appendix A).
    1478             :  *
    1479             :  * The reason why we have to differentiate between the TAB and the MIF font
    1480             :  * style values is that in TAB, TABFSBox is included in the style value
    1481             :  * as code 0x100, but in MIF it is not included, instead it is implied by
    1482             :  * the presence of the BG color in the FONT() clause (the BG color is
    1483             :  * present only when TABFSBox or TABFSHalo is set).
    1484             :  * This also has the effect of shifting all the other style values > 0x100
    1485             :  * by 1 byte.
    1486             :  *
    1487             :  * NOTE: Even if there is no BG color for font symbols, we inherit this
    1488             :  * problem because Font Point styles use the same codes as Text Font styles.
    1489             :  **********************************************************************/
    1490           0 : int TABFontPoint::GetFontStyleMIFValue()
    1491             : {
    1492             :     // The conversion is simply to remove bit 0x100 from the value and shift
    1493             :     // down all values past this bit.
    1494           0 :     return (m_nFontStyle & 0xff) + (m_nFontStyle & (0xff00 - 0x0100)) / 2;
    1495             : }
    1496             : 
    1497         635 : void TABFontPoint::SetFontStyleMIFValue(int nStyle)

    4945             : 
    4946             :     /*-------------------------------------------------------------
    4947             :      * OK, Arc angles again!!!!!!!!!!!!
    4948             :      * After some tests in 1999-11, it appeared that the angle values
    4949             :      * ALWAYS had to be flipped (read order= end angle followed by
    4950             :      * start angle), no matter which quadrant the file is in.
    4951             :      * This does not make any sense, so I suspect that there is something
    4952             :      * that we are missing here!
    4953             :      *
    4954             :      * 2000-01-14.... Again!!!  Based on some sample data files:
    4955             :      *  File         Ver Quadr  ReflXAxis  Read_Order   Adjust_Angle

    8137             :  *                   ITABFeaturePen::SetPenWidthPixel()
    8138             :  *                   ITABFeaturePen::GetPenWidthPoint()
    8139             :  *                   ITABFeaturePen::SetPenWidthPoint()
    8140             :  *
    8141             :  * Pen width can be expressed in pixels (value from 1 to 7 pixels) or
    8142             :  * in points (value from 0.1 to 203.7 points). The default pen width
    8143             :  * in MapInfo is 1 pixel.  Pen width in points exist only in file version 450.
    8144             :  *
    8145             :  * The following methods hide the way the pen width is stored in the files.
    8146             :  *
    8147             :  * In order to establish if a given pen def had its width specified in
    8148             :  * pixels or in points, one should first call GetPenWidthPoint(), and if
    8149             :  * it returns 0 then the Pixel width should be used instead:
    8150             :  *    if (GetPenWidthPoint() == 0)
    8151             :  *       ... use pen width in points ...
    8152             :  *    else
    8153             :  *       ... use Pixel width from GetPenWidthPixel()
    8154             :  *
    8155             :  * Note that the reverse is not true: the default pixel width is always 1,
    8156             :  * even when the pen width was actually set in points.
